                          4
Who am I?
My name is Jalal Sameja, and you all know me for my Delicious
Recipes behind Jalalsamfit. I’ve always grown up with family around
me and some of my fondest childhood memories have been at the
dinner table with big family gatherings enjoying delicious meals
together. This instilled in me a love for food and going through these
experiences has shaped me into the man I am today. As a teenager,
I struggled with weight and turned to fitness and weightlifting for
a healthier lifestyle.

I began to learn about nutrition, macros, calorie deficit - everything
to help me lose body fat. This also pushed me to start making meals
for myself, but my goal to lose weight also sacrificed my love for
delicious tasting meals because I used to believe that good tasting
food = unhealthy/bad for you. Before long, I started to realise that
I do not enjoy eating such bland meals and I could not sustain this
long term. I began to experiment by combining the knowledge I
gathered on nutrition with my love for food and cooking. Through
lots of trial and error, hours spent in the kitchen - I learnt techniques
to merge the best of both worlds. Learning that you do not need to
sacrifice taste and flavour to lead a Healthier Lifestyle and with a
few simple ingredient swaps it was very possible to make the Most
Delicious High Protein Meals that you can have year round! And
My Mission is to continue to share all of this knowledge with you
through all these Recipes and Much More!

  minutes. Remove the chicken and set aside, cooking
  in batches if necessary.




 IMPORTANT COOKING NOTES
 z   Mix chicken thoroughly until dark and rich in color. Add more spices or soy sauce if needed.
 z   Avoid overcrowding the pan to ensure a crispy crust on the chicken.
 z   Bake fries for 25 minutes or air fry for 15 minutes at 210°C (420°F).
 z   Reheat fries in a pan or air fryer to restore crispiness.

 z   Marinate steak bites for at least 10–15 minutes for deeper flavor.
 z   Cook on medium-high heat for 2–3 minutes per side in butter until nicely charred. Avoid overcrowding for a

 z   Prepare the sauce in advance and store in a bottle for future meals.

 z   Reheat only the potatoes and beef since the pico is stored separately.

 z   Marinate the chicken overnight for maximum flavor, ensuring each piece is well coated on both sides.

 IMPORTANT COOKING NOTES
 z   Marinate the chicken overnight for the best flavor, but 10–15 minutes works if short on time.
 z   Use fresh tomatoes instead of canned to reduce acidity and add natural sweetness.
 z   Let the sauce cool before blending to prevent pressure buildup and spills.
 z   Turn off the heat before adding yogurt to keep the sauce smooth and prevent curdling.

 z   Cook the chicken on high heat, stirring frequently to develop a golden brown color. Once browned, add the
     sauce on medium heat, let it thicken, then remove from heat with all the sauce.
 z   When cooking the vegetables, make sure the carrots have fully softened before adding the rice.

Why I Use Grams (g) as My Main Form of Measurement
When it comes to meal prepping and cooking with precision, I prefer to use grams (g) as the
standard unit of measurement. Why? The reason is simple: grams give you a much more accurate
and consistent way to measure ingredients. Unlike cups or tablespoons, which can vary in volume
depending on how ingredients are packed or even the brand you use, grams are always the same.
For example, 100 grams of chicken breast will always weigh the same, no matter the size of the
breast or the way it's cut. This consistency is key when you're trying to hit specific macro or calorie
goals, especially for fitness-focused meal plans. Using grams ensures that you're tracking your food
intake more accurately, which is vital for those working on weight loss, muscle gain, or any other
specific nutritional goals.
Additionally, grams help with portion control, ensuring you don’t overestimate or underestimate
the amounts you’re consuming. It also simplifies scaling recipes, so you can easily adjust them
depending on how many servings you need.




                                                 220
                                                                  THE MEAL PREP COOK BOOK




 How to Track Macros & Calories for These Meals
 Tracking your macros (proteins, carbs, fats) and calories is a great way to make sure your
 meals align with your fitness or nutrition goals. Here's a simple approach to keep things
 organized and accurate:
 – Start with a Food Scale: For precision, always weigh your ingredients.
   Use a digital scale for the most accurate readings in grams. If
   you don’t have a scale, most food packaging will have nutritional
   information based on weight (such as per 100g or per serving).
 – Use a Reliable App or Calculator: There are several apps like MyFitnessPal,
   Cronometer, or Carb Manager, where you can log your meals and track calories
   and macros. These apps allow you to input your meals by scanning barcodes
   or manually entering ingredients. They provide detailed breakdowns of the
   nutritional content per item and will help you keep track of your daily intake.
 – Calculate Your Needs: Before you start tracking, it’s important to know how many
   calories and what macro ratio (protein, carbs, fats) you should aim for each day. This
   will vary depending on whether you're trying to lose weight, gain muscle, or maintain
   your current weight. There are plenty of online calculators available that can help you
   determine these numbers based on factors like age, weight, activity level, and goals.
 – Adjust Serving Sizes for Your Goals: Each recipe in this cookbook has the nutrition
   information based on the specific serving size. However, you might want to adjust
   the serving size depending on your goals. If you're eating less or more than the
   standard portion, be sure to adjust the calories and macros accordingly.
 – Consistency is Key: The most important tip when tracking your macros and
   calories is to be consistent. Track every meal, even snacks, and ensure you're
   measuring everything to maintain accuracy. Over time, you'll get better at
   estimating portions, but in the beginning, it's best to be as precise as possible.
 Tracking your macros and calories can feel overwhelming at first, but with a little practice, it
 becomes second nature. Plus, it will give you a much clearer understanding of what you’re
 putting into your body and how it’s helping you reach your goals.
